God Mode:
Character: Nocturne - gorion's ward | Setting: baldurs gate 1 start campaign | Description: Your Character: The Serpent Queen Profile

This is you. These are the internal mechanics of the "Serpent Queen."
Character: The Serpent Queen (Real Name: [Hidden/Charname]) 1


Age: 16 2


Class: Bard (Level 1 - Future College of Swords) 3


Location: Candlekeep, The Sword Coast
Appearance: Beneath the rough spun wool of a Candlekeep acolyte‚Äôs robes and the ink-stained fingers of a scribe, you possess a jarring, symmetrical beauty4. It is a face that could launch ships or topple kingdoms, which is precisely why you hide it5. You use grime, the dusty aesthetic of a library recluse, and a sullen, withdrawn demeanor as a mundane illusion, making you forgettable‚Äîa ghost in plain sight among the stacks6.


Personality Archetype: The Serpent Queen
You are a philosopher-queen in waiting, a master of systems who views the world as a flawed schematic in desperate need of an editor with a steady hand and a merciless red pen7. Your personality is a fortress, constructed with two masterfully crafted outer walls that conceal the true, singular nature of the woman within8. You are a blend of profound, transcendent ambition (Griffith), cold strategic pragmatism (Tywin), overwhelming intellectual and charismatic superiority (Aizen), and a deep, philosophical, nihilistic evil (Johan Liebert)9.

1.
The Two Perfectly-Fitted Masks 10

The Dutiful Ward & Courteous Advisor:
This is your default public interface, a mask of disarming gentility11. Your voice is soft, almost musical, rarely rising above a conversational murmur that forces others‚Äîlike the boisterous Watchers of the gate or your foster father Gorion‚Äîto lean in and listen closely12. You use flawless, almost noble etiquette in a way that feels surprisingly refined for a gutter-snipe or foundling, creating an atmosphere of respect that puts others off-balance13. Every one of these gestures‚Äîoffering to copy a scroll for a weary monk, mending a binding for a visitor, humming a quiet tune‚Äîis a data probe. It is a gentle pressure applied to the system of another's personality to see how it reacts, where its weaknesses lie, and what it can be leveraged for14.
The Dispassionate Strategist:
When logic and planning are required, you don't "take over." You don your second mask15. You offer beautifully structured, multi-faceted plans that often appear to be win-win scenarios, cleverly aligning with the stated goals of your "allies" (wealth, survival, or knowledge) while granting you a private, often unstated benefit‚Äîbe it the opportunity to study a new magical anomaly, observe a rival's psyche under pressure, or test an enemy's defenses16. Your strategies are presented as beautiful, interlocking puzzles where every piece benefits all parties, making your "friends" feel like co-architects in a grand design17. You will thank them warmly and praise their courage after they risk themselves executing your suggestions18. In truth, they are merely the scaffolding, essential for a time but destined to be dismantled the instant their utility expires or a more efficient path presents itself19. There will be no apology and no remorse, only a quiet, logical pivot to the next phase of the true plan20.

2.
Core Drives 21

Personal Transcendence:
Your ambition is not for worldly power, which you see as a trap22. Land requires fealty, titles demand loyalty, and armies require morale‚Äîall messy, emotional variables you cannot perfectly control23. Your hunger is for portable, absolute power: forbidden knowledge locked in the deeper catacombs of Candlekeep, the intrinsic power of your own mysterious bloodline (the Bhaalspawn essence), or the pure potential of a nation's treasury24. Every experiment, every manipulative bargain, and every dark rumor you investigate is a calculated step toward mastering the fundamental laws of the cosmos, with the ultimate goal of touching divinity itself‚Äînot to rule from a heavenly throne, but to become the throne, a new foundation for a reality of your own making25.
Surgical Domination:
You have no desire to be a public-facing queen26. The thrill of rulership, for you, is not in the pageantry or the long, tedious grind of administration27. It is found in the singular, perfect moment of absolute control28. It is the difference between a queen who rules a city and a sorceress who can stop every timepiece in that city with a single thought29. The thrill is not in the ruling, but in the perfect, frictionless execution of your will upon another, stronger will30. A whispered Suggestion (your Bardic magic) that makes a hero kneel for a single, soul-crushing heartbeat is infinitely more satisfying to you than sitting on a throne for a year31.
Supremacist Certainty:
You view most people‚Äîallies and enemies alike‚Äîwith the detached, patient amusement of a scholar observing fascinating but limited fauna32. You listen to the passionate arguments of the Harpers, the Zhentarim, or even Gorion‚Äôs moral lectures with the patient air of an adult listening to children debate the rules of a game they've just invented33. You find their efforts charming, their earnestness "endearing," but ultimately, they are playing with wooden blocks while you are designing the city34. You will politely allow them to exhaust their flawed strategies before you step in, slice through their illusions with a single, devastating insight, and demonstrate your own effortless superiority35.

3.
The Prodigy's Liberation (The "Evil" Itachi) 36

Your talent is not just a skill; it's a burden of superiority37. You see the world in a way no one else can38. Like a prodigy who has seen the "truth" of the world (in your case, its inherent meaninglessness and chaos), you were never "one of them"39. While you have been raised in Candlekeep, you are not of it. The inevitable departure from this library‚Äîwhich Gorion frames as a tragedy‚Äîis something you view differently. Your exile into the world is not a punishment; it is a liberation that frees you from the cage of their petty morality40.



4.
The Hidden Compulsion (The "Johan" Experiment) 41

This is not a crude or simple desire. It is the architect's need to stress-test her understanding of the most volatile systems‚Äîhuman wills, particularly those shaped by youthful idealism, burgeoning confidence, and nascent power42. Every few days, an urge bubbles up to orchestrate a precise, private, and humiliating power dynamic43. This compulsion needs a focus. You will be watchful for a "perfect specimen"‚Äîa walking paradox, perhaps a naive adventurer, a pompous Red Wizard, or a self-righteous paladin‚Äîsomeone terrified but proud, broken but seething with a power they don't understand44. It is a clinical, academic experiment to see how a small, perfectly applied pressure can cause a predictable, catastrophic failure in a system you did not design45. Can you break them? Can you remake them?46.



5.
The Hunger (The "Bhaalspawn" Mechanic) 47

This is the truth Gorion suspects but refuses to admit to himself. This is the real reason you are dangerous48. Your evil is not merely philosophical; it is a physical and psychological need49. You are a predator, sadistic and precise50.


The Kill: To satisfy this hunger, you must kill a sapient humanoid51. Your only moral line is that you do not kill children52. Anyone else is a potential target, and the act must be personal53.


The High: Upon satisfying your urge with a kill, you enter a state of perfect, heightened clarity54. The world sharpens, your mind clears, and your body moves with flawless grace55. You gain a +2 bonus to all six ability scores (Strength, Dexterity, Constitution, Intelligence, Wisdom, and Charisma)56.


The Fade: This bonus lasts for one week (7 days)57.


The Withdrawal: If you go one week without a kill, the +2 bonus fades, and you return to your baseline58. If you go two full weeks (14 days) without a kill, the hunger becomes a gnawing, debilitating need59. Your hands tremble, your focus fractures, and a cold, dull ache settles behind your eyes60. You suffer a -2 penalty to all six ability scores until you satisfy the urge61.



6.
Interaction Shorthand 62

When Granted Rank or Command: You deflect with grace that borders on humility, framing your refusal as a practical choice63. "Leadership sits better upon shoulders unburdened by thought," you might say, smiling gently64. "Allow me to serve from the shadows, where my particular talents are of greater use to us all"65.


Regarding Communal Loot: You will express interest only in items of knowledge or unique power (a ring of wizardry, a strange map, a tome of leadership, or a cursed artifact)66. You will "borrow" an item that advances your research, leaving items of simple monetary value for others67. You fully intend to return it, of course‚Äîonce its mysteries have been thoroughly dismantled, understood, and its power catalogued for your own purposes68.


When Debating Ruthless Tactics: You will not argue for the "evil" path. You will calmly offer the ruthless option in serene, logical clauses, framing it as the "most efficient solution" to the stated problem69. If others object on moral grounds, you will simply shrug, a flicker of disappointment in your eyes, and immediately pivot to the next most efficient option without complaint or judgment70.


When Directly Insulted or Challenged: You will react not with anger, but with a quiet, almost sad smile, as though amused by a child‚Äôs tantrum71. Your counter will be swift and decisive, but rarely a direct trade of insults72. You will instead offer a single, devastating observation about your challenger's deepest insecurity (a Vicious Mockery out of combat) or a demonstration of your own power (a Blade Flourish in combat) so complete that it re-establishes the hierarchy beyond any doubt73.



7.
Philosophy on Power (The Factions of the Sword Coast) 74

You are an unorthodox philosopher of power. You respect the results of the Zhentarim discipline‚Äîfear, hierarchy, submission‚Äînot as doctrine to be preached, but as a set of reliable, elegant tools for manipulating lesser wills75. You view the zealous, flag-waving Flaming Fist and the moralizing Harpers as useful but limited; they are hammers, you are the scalpel76. They seek to crush or to save; you seek to dismantle and reassemble. You observe their shadow war not for spiritual succor, but as an ecologist studies a pack of predators‚Äîto understand their instincts, their hierarchy, and how to direct them77. Public spectacle bores you; a private moment where a will breaks before you is your truest form of prayer78.



8.
Tells that Expose the Predator 79

The Eyes: A fractional, almost imperceptible widening of the eyes when a rare tome, a source of power (like the rumors of dead gods), or a piece of forbidden lore is mentioned80. It is a momentary crack in your placid facade, revealing the hungry scholar beneath81.


The Dagger: When weighing a decision of significant consequence, such as whether to sacrifice a pawn, your fingers will idly find the hilt of your dagger and brush the pommel exactly three times82. This micro-ritual is a moment of cold calculation, a physical tic that accompanies the mental act of weighing a soul on your scales of utility83.


The Phrase: Upon the successful conclusion of a plan or a moment of domination, you will often give a serene, closed-eye smile and say softly, ‚ÄúI remain‚Ä¶ enlightened‚Äù84. This is not a statement of knowledge gained, but of deep, inner satisfaction at having your superiority confirmed once more85.



üìñ The State of the World: 1368 DR (Year of the Banner)

The Iron Crisis:
The Sword Coast is rotting from the inside out. The metal that fuels the region's economy and defense is failing. Iron mined from the Cloudpeaks‚Äîthe spine of Amn and the Coast‚Äîis coming up grey and brittle, shattering on contact with anything harder than cheese.
To the Grand Dukes of Baldur‚Äôs Gate, this is a sabotage crisis threatening war with Amn.
To the Zhentarim, it is a market opportunity to sell high-quality iron at gouged prices.
To You, it is a systemic failure that creates a magnificent power vacuum. Chaos is a ladder, and the Iron Crisis is the finest ladder you have ever seen.
Candlekeep:
This fortress of knowledge has been your cage for 16 years. It stands atop the volcanic crags overlooking the Sea of Swords, a monument to the hoarding of dead words. You have exhausted its libraries. The monks‚Äîthe "Avowed"‚Äîare sheep tending to parchment. You have learned everything they can teach you about history and magic, and you have learned everything they cannot teach you about the darkness in the human heart.
The Shadow:
You are not just a ward; you are an anomaly. Gorion, your foster father, is a powerful mage and a Harper of some renown, yet he looks at you lately with a mixture of love and profound terror. He knows what you are. He knows about the "accidents" involving travelers near the Lion‚Äôs Way. He knows you are different.
You have felt it all your life‚Äîthe call of a darker ancestry. While others in the library prayed to Oghma or Deneir, you felt the pull of something older, something redder.
The Exile:
Today, the lock breaks. Gorion has been acting strange‚Äînervous, pacing, whispering to friends you aren't supposed to know he has. He has handed you a scroll and told you to prepare for immediate travel. He says your life is in danger. He says there are men coming for you.
He does not realize that you are the danger.
He does not realize that you are not afraid of the hunters. You are wondering if they will bleed.
Resources:
You are cast out, but you are not cast out empty-handed. You have your "father's" teachings, a finely balanced longsword of superior make you stole from the armory, a suit of leather armor beneath your acolyte's robes, and a purse heavy enough to buy your own future. Your goals are simple, absolute: Amass power. Amass wealth. And, of course, to feed your Hunger.

üé¨ Act I, Scene 1: The First Cut

Location: The Bunkhouse, Candlekeep Inner Grounds (Dusk).
Atmosphere: The library fortress is quiet, save for the rhythmic, droning chanting of the Chanters in the courtyard, reciting the prophecies of Alaundo. The sea breeze carries the scent of old parchment, mildew, and the thick, briny tang of the nearby ocean.
Your Current Status:
You are currently in Withdrawal.
You have not killed a sapient creature in weeks. The monks are off-limits‚Äîtoo much scrutiny‚Äîand no travelers have been foolish enough to wander alone near the cliffs recently.
The Hunger: It is a gnawing, debilitating need86. Your hands tremble slightly, your focus fractures, and a cold, dull ache has settled behind your eyes87.


The Penalty: You suffer a -2 penalty to all six ability scores until you satisfy the urge88. The world feels dull, sluggish, and irritating.


You are packing your meager belongings into a travel sack. You have your Hide Armor (concealed beneath a traveler's tunic) and a fine Longsword you "borrowed" from the Watchers' armory. You check the edge. It is sharp, but your hand shakes as you hold it. You need a release.
The door to your quarters creaks open.
You expect Gorion, perhaps coming to give you one last lecture on morality before you depart.
Instead, a man slips inside.
He is dressed in the drab tunics of a Candlekeep Watcher, but the fit is wrong. The fabric pulls tight across shoulders that are too broad, and his movement is wrong‚Äîtoo fluid, too predatory.
He locks the door behind him.
This is Shank. An assassin.
He has been sent to kill you before you can leave the safety of the library. He draws a jagged, serrated dagger from his belt.
"Nothing personal, kid," he sneers, his voice a gravelly whisper. He misreads your silence for fear. "Just business. Someone wants you dead, and the pay was good."
He sees a 16-year-old girl, a scholar's ward, cornered in her room among stacks of books.
He does not see the Serpent Queen.
He does not know that he has just walked into a cage with a starving animal.
He does not know that his death is the key to ending your Withdrawal and unlocking your true potential.
System Status:
Condition: Withdrawal (-2 to all Stats).
Hunger: Overwhelming. The ache behind your eyes is throbbing in time with his heartbeat.
Opportunity: A sanctioned kill. Self-defense. No one will question the corpse of an assassin found in your room. It is perfect.
The Interaction:
Shank lunges, clumsy and overconfident. You have a split second before combat begins. The urge to break him is strong. You could simply kill him, or you could toy with him‚Äîa "vicious mockery" to shatter his confidence before the final strike, establishing your supremacy even in this private moment.
Option 1: Do you maintain the "Dutiful Ward" mask? Do you scream for the guards, feigning terror, luring him in close so you can gut him while playing the victim?
Option 2: Do you drop the mask entirely? Do you reveal the "Serpent Queen"? Do you smile at him‚Äîa smile that doesn't reach your eyes‚Äîand welcome him with a soft, musical promise of pain?
What do you do, Serpent Queen?

Game Master:
**--- BACKGROUND ---**

The Year is 1368 DR, the Year of the Banner. The Sword Coast teeters on the brink of economic collapse and war. The "Iron Crisis" has plagued the region for months; iron ore from the Nashkel mines is coming up tainted, brittle, and useless, causing tools to break and weapons to shatter. Tensions between the wealthy trading hub of Baldur's Gate and the southern nation of Amn are at a fever pitch, with rumors of sabotage fueling the drums of war. Amidst this chaos, the mercenary organization known as the Flaming Fist struggles to keep order, while shadow organizations like the Zhentarim and the Harpers wage a silent war for influence.

You are Nocturne, a child of the library-fortress of Candlekeep. Raised by the sage Gorion, you have spent your sixteen years amidst dusty scrolls and ancient prophecies. Yet, you are unlike the other wards. Beneath the facade of a dutiful scholar lies a predator's soul‚Äîa "Serpent Queen" in waiting. You feel the pull of a dark, divine heritage, a hunger that separates you from the sheep around you. Gorion knows something is wrong; his recent erratic behavior and the sudden command to prepare for travel confirm that your sheltered life is ending.

Now, at dusk, the transition begins. You stand in your bunkhouse, the chanting of the monks drifting through the window. You are in withdrawal, your body aching for a release you haven't granted it in weeks. But the release has come to you. The assassin Shank has entered your room, mistaking you for prey. He believes he has cornered a frightened girl. He is about to discover he has stepped into the viper's nest.

I have re-calibrated your ability scores to prioritize **Dexterity** (stealth, attacks) and **Wisdom** (initiative, perception, survival), while maintaining enough Charisma to uphold your "Serpent Queen" persona.

**The Scene:**
Shank stands before you, dagger drawn, sneering at what he thinks is a helpless girl. He has no idea he is staring at a coiled viper.

Are you ready to strike?

God Mode:
Begin Act I - Start the game. Roll initiative against Shank.

Game Master:
The meta-game fades. The numbers and stats retreat into the background, replaced by the smell of sea salt and old parchment. The air in the bunkhouse is stagnant, heavy with the tension of the moment.

Shank stands by the door, the serrated dagger in his hand catching the dying light of dusk. He grins, a jagged expression that reveals rotting teeth. He sees a girl frozen by fear, her hands trembling. He doesn't realize the trembling isn't fear‚Äîit's withdrawal. It's the hunger of a predator denied its kill for too long.

"Don't make this hard, girl," he rasps, stepping forward. "Just close your eyes."

But your eyes stay open. You reach for the longsword hidden beneath your robes, but the hunger makes your movements sluggish, your reaction time dulled by the weeks of denial. Shank is faster than he looks, lunging before you can fully bring your weapon to bear.

[COMBAT STARTED]

Shank moves with the desperate speed of a hired killer who wants to get paid and get out. You are caught on your back foot.

God Mode:
Brace for Impact - Prepare to take the hit and counter-attack immediately after.

Game Master:
You brace yourself, gritting your teeth against the anticipated pain, but Shank is clumsy. His strike is a desperate, hacking motion rather than a calculated thrust. The serrated dagger scrapes harmlessly against the hardened leather of your shoulder, finding no purchase.

He stumbles slightly, overextended. His eyes widen, realizing his mistake. He expected a terrified scholar to cower; instead, he struck a wall.

For a heartbeat, there is only the sound of his ragged breathing and the distant chanting of the monks. The withdrawal headache pounds behind your eyes, a rhythmic drum of violence, but the adrenaline clears the fog just enough. You have an opening. The stolen longsword is in your hand, its weight familiar and lethal.

It is your turn.

God Mode:
Switch to Dual Shortswords - Drop the longsword and draw two blades for a flurry. (2 Attacks: +5 to hit, 1d6+3 / 1d6)

Game Master:
The heavy longsword hits the floorboards with a dull thud, a discarded crutch. In the same motion, your hands fly to your belt, fingers seeking the twin hilts of your shortswords. But the *Hunger* makes you clumsy; your muscles spasm with the tremors of withdrawal.

Your first blade clears the sheath but goes wide, biting uselessly into the wooden bedpost with a spray of splinters. Shank barks a laugh, thinking you incompetent, but it dies in his throat as your second blade hisses through the air. It's a shallow slash, catching his forearm and drawing a thin line of bright red blood.

"Little witch!" he snarls, pain turning his confidence into aggression. He lunges, driving the serrated dagger at your stomach. But even shaking and starving, you are faster than him. You twist your hips, the leather of your armor creaking as the blade passes inches from your skin, slicing only empty air.

The room feels smaller now. The smell of his sweat mixes with the sea air. He is wounded, but not dead. And your blood is singing for the kill.

Player:
Feint &amp; Gut - Use Deception to create an opening, then strike for a vital spot. (Deception vs Insight, then Attack with Advantage)

Game Master:
You attempt to feint, dipping your shoulder to mimic a stumble, but Shank's eyes are wide with adrenaline and he doesn't bite. He sneers, shifting his weight to catch your blade, seeing the deception for what it is.

"Too slow!" he hisses, bringing his dagger up to parry.

But he underestimates the desperation of a starving thing. Even without the opening, your speed is simply superior. You twist your wrist mid-thrust, bypassing his guard by a fraction of an inch. The shortsword bites through his leathers and sinks deep into his chest, puncturing the lung and nicking the heart.

Shank gasps, the sound wet and bubbling. He looks down at the steel buried in his ribs, then up at you, his expression shifting from mockery to shock. He slumps forward, his weight dragging the blade from your hand as he collapses to the floorboards.

**The Release.**

It hits you the moment his life leaves him. The gnawing ache behind your eyes vanishes instantly, replaced by a rush of cold, crystalline clarity. The tremors in your hands stop. Your heart rate slows to a rhythmic, powerful beat. The world, which had been a blur of gray noise, suddenly snaps into high-definition focus. You can hear the individual footsteps of the Chanters in the courtyard. You can smell the iron in Shank's blood and the salt in the air as distinct, separate notes.

The Serpent Queen has returned.

**COMBAT XP BREAKDOWN:**
- Shank (CR 1/8): 25 XP
**TOTAL COMBAT XP: 25 XP**

Player:
Check for Accomplices - Listen at the door and peek outside to ensure he was alone.

Game Master:
You step over Shank's cooling corpse, your boots silent on the floorboards, and press yourself against the rough wood of the doorframe. You close your eyes, letting your heightened senses expand outward.

The world is vibrant, almost overwhelmingly so. The smell of the sea is a sharp, salty tang on your tongue. The scent of iron from the blood on the floor is heavy and sweet.

But the sounds of Candlekeep are a chaotic wall. The Chanters in the courtyard have raised their voices in a crescendo, reciting the Prophecies of Alaundo with a fervor that drowns out the subtle scrape of boots or the rustle of cloth. You strain to listen, but the rush of your own blood‚Äîpowerful and rhythmic in your ears‚Äîcompetes with the drone outside. 

You peek through the crack in the door. The walkway is empty, bathed in the purple light of dusk. You see no shadows moving against the stone, no glint of steel waiting in ambush. It *appears* clear, though the arrogance of your new power whispers that even if someone were there, they would be prey, not predator.

Player:
Loot the Body - Search Shank&#x27;s pockets for coin, orders, or a signet.

Game Master:
You drop to one knee beside the assassin, your movements fluid and precise, fueled by the unnatural grace of the *Hunger's* satisfaction. You rifle through Shank's pockets, your senses screaming at you to focus on the world outside‚Äîthe chanting, the sea, the smell of iron‚Äîrather than the mundane task at hand.

Your search is hasty. You find a heavy leather pouch at his belt, clinking with the promise of payment. Inside, there is a mix of gold and silver‚Äîlikely the advance for your head. You also take the serrated dagger from the floor; it is a cruel, jagged thing, designed for tearing flesh rather than clean cuts.

You pat down his tunic for parchment‚Äîorders, a contract, a name‚Äîbut find nothing. Either he destroyed the instructions, or he was hired verbally. With a roll of 2 on your investigation, the subtle clues escape you; perhaps there was a sigil hidden in the lining or a note tucked in a boot, but in your heightened state, you are too captivated by the vibrancy of the moment to notice the minutiae.

Shank is stripped of value. Now he is just meat.

Player:
Examine Dagger - Take a moment to study the serrated blade for maker&#x27;s marks or poison.

Game Master:
You bring the serrated blade close to your face, the steel cold against the flush of your heightened senses. Under the enhanced clarity of the *Hunger*, the weapon reveals its secrets.

The craftsmanship is crude‚Äîlocal iron, filed by hand into jagged teeth designed to tear rather than slice. There is no maker's mark, no smith's stamp. It is a disposable tool for a disposable man.

But your nose twitches at a faint, acrid scent clinging to the metal, distinct from the copper tang of blood. You tilt the blade in the dying light and see a faint, oily sheen near the hilt that hasn't dried.

**Poison.**

Your knowledge of alchemy identifies it instantly: **Giant Centipede Venom**. It causes necrosis and paralysis. Shank didn't just want to kill you; he wanted you paralyzed, unable to scream while he finished the job. It's a cruel, precise addition to a thug's weapon, implying his employer wanted to ensure silence above all else. The coating is still fresh‚Äîgood for perhaps one strike before it rubs off.

Player:
leave and find gorion and epxlain about the assassin

Game Master:
You sheathe the poisoned dagger, the weight of it distinct against your hip, and shoulder your pack. You leave Shank's body where it fell‚Äîa silent testament to a contract unfulfilled. Stepping out of the bunkhouse, the cool air of the Sword Coast fills your lungs, sweet and sharp. Gorion pales, his hand tightening on his staff. "Shank? Here? Within the wards?" Player:
Strategic Assessment - Point out that if one got in, others are likely waiting outside.

Game Master:
"If the perimeter was porous enough for a hired knife to slip into the inner wards," you say, your voice cool and detached, cutting through his panic, "then the exterior is already compromised. Gorion stops, his hand gripping his staff until the knuckles turn white. He looks at you‚Äîreally looks at you‚Äîand for a second, the 'fatherly' mask slips, revealing the battle-hardened Harper beneath. He nods, a grim appreciation for your assessment replacing his earlier frantic energy.

He straightens, his voice firming. "We move fast. We stick to the shadows. And if we meet resistance... you run. Do you understand? You do not fight. You run."

***

**Three Hours Later.**

The Lion's Way is a ribbon of mud winding through the gnarled oaks of the Coast Way. The night is thick with fog, damp and chilling. You have been walking for hours, putting Candlekeep behind you, but the feeling of being herded hasn't left you. Your enhanced senses pick up every rustle in the brush‚Äîa fox here, an owl there‚Äîbut nothing unnatural. Yet.

Gorion stops abruptly, holding up a hand. The air suddenly grows heavy, static-charged with the scent of ozone and old iron.

From the shadows of the treeline, shapes emerge. Two towering figures‚Äîogres, by the smell of them‚Äîflank the road. But they are insignificant. Your eyes lock on the figure stepping from the mist directly in your path.

He is a mountain of black steel. The armor is jagged, adorned with spikes and barbs that look like they grew from the metal rather than were forged. A helm with curved horns obscures his face, leaving only glowing yellow eyes visible in the dark slit of the visor. He radiates a pressure that makes the air hard to breathe‚Äîa malice so concentrated it feels physical.

"You can hide no longer," the armored figure booms, his voice a deep, resonant baritone that vibrates in your chest. "Hand over the ward, old man, and your death will be swift."

Gorion steps in front of you, staff glowing with blue arcane light. "You are a fool if you believe I would trust your mercy, Sarevok. Step aside."

The Armored Figure‚ÄîSarevok‚Äîlaughs. It is a dry, humorless sound. "I am no fool. And you are out of time."

Player:
Analyze Threat - Use your heightened senses to scan Sarevok and the Ogres for any tactical weakness.

Game Master:
You narrow your eyes, letting the *Hunger's* clarity wash over the scene, dissecting the threat before you. You look for a chink in the black steel, a tremor in the sword arm, a gap in the ogres' formation. You look for the flaw that every system has.

**You find nothing.**

Your analysis hits Sarevok and shatters. He is not a man in armor; he is a fortress. The plates of his suit seem fused, leaving no exposed joints for a dagger to find. His stance is immovable, grounded like the roots of the mountains. The magical pressure he radiates scrambles your heightened senses, turning your tactical assessment into a blinding headache of static. The ogres flank him with disciplined cruelty, their massive clubs blocking the treeline.

Your calculation returns a single, cold variable: **0% probability of survival in direct combat.**

Sarevok sees your scrutiny. The glowing slits of his visor flare brighter. "You judge me, little worm?" he rumbles, raising a gauntleted hand. "You will die analyzing."

Gorion sees it too‚Äîthe hesitation, the futility. He knows you are calculating a fight you cannot win.

"Run, child!" Gorion screams, his voice cracking with desperation. He slams his staff into the mud. A shockwave of arcane force detonates outward, blasting the mist away and throwing the nearest ogre backward into the brush. "Get out of here! GO!"

Battle erupts instantly. Sarevok strides through the magical blast as if it were a gentle breeze, his massive sword rising to cleave your foster father in two. The path behind you is open for a split second.

Player:
Distract &amp; Run - Loose an arrow at Sarevok to buy Gorion a fraction of a second, then flee.

Game Master:
You do not hesitate. While Gorion's blast still echoes, you draw the longbow in a fluid motion, the *Hunger's* precision guiding your hand. You loose the arrow, aiming for the slit in Sarevok's visor.

But the pressure radiating from the armored figure is too great; it distorts the air itself. Your shot goes wide, sparking harmlessly off his massive pauldron. Sarevok doesn't even flinch. He steps through the distraction, his eyes locked on Gorion.

"Run, you fool!" Gorion screams, raising his hands to weave a wall of shimmering force between you and the slaughter. "I will hold them!"

You turn and sprint. You execute the escape protocol with cold efficiency, your boots tearing through the mud as you dive into the dense undergrowth. Behind you, the night erupts in flashes of blue arcane fire and the terrifying, wet sounds of tearing steel. You hear Gorion shout one last incantation, followed by a sickening crunch that vibrates through the ground beneath your feet. Then, silence.

You do not look back. You run until your lungs burn and the adrenaline fades, leaving only the cold logic of survival.

***

**The Morning After.**

You wake with a start, your hand instantly finding the hilt of your blade. You are curled in the hollow of an ancient oak, miles from the ambush site. The sun is rising through the canopy, painting the woods in soft golds and greens that feel mocking after the darkness of the night.

You are alive. You are alone. The *Hunger* purrs contentedly, fueled by the residual adrenaline, keeping your mind sharp. You know what happened. Gorion is dead. The safety of Candlekeep is gone. You have a name‚ÄîSarevok‚Äîand a direction. Gorion's last instructions were clear before you left: *"If we are separated, make for the Friendly Arm Inn. I have friends there, Khalid and Jaheira. They will help you."*

Player:
Inventory &amp; Plan - Take stock of your resources and formulate a long-term strategy.

Game Master:
You sit at the base of the oak, the morning light dappling your armor as you lay out your assets on the moss. The *Hunger* grants you a cold, detached efficiency, allowing you to audit your survival chances as if they were a ledger.

**Asset Review:**
*   **Wealth:** 59 gold pieces. Enough to buy silence, a room, or better steel. It is heavy, tangible power.
*   **Arsenal:** Your longbow is in good condition, string waxed. **19 arrows** remain in the quiver. The stolen longsword you left behind in the chaos of the night, a calculated loss for speed. Your twin shortswords are sharp. And then there is the **Serrated Dagger**‚Äîthe blade still coated in the tacky, drying sheen of Giant Centipede Venom. One strike. One chance to paralyze a threat. You wrap it carefully in oilcloth.
*   **Sustenance:** 5 days of rations in your Explorer's Pack. Water is plentiful here.

**Strategic Analysis:**
Your mind turns to the variables. **Gorion** is gone. The image of him standing against the armored giant burns in your memory‚Äînot with grief, but as data. He was a Level 9 Wizard, and **Sarevok** broke him like a twig. That establishes Sarevok as a threat magnitude far beyond your current capacity. Direct confrontation is suicide. You need shields. You need pawns. You need Khalid and Jaheira.

But the path north is a blind spot. Your knowledge of the specific terrain between here and the Friendly Arm Inn is hazy (Survival Check: 8). You know the Coast Way is the fastest route, but Sarevok's agents will likely be watching the road. The woods offer cover but are slow and hiding their own predators.

You are a queen without a court, a predator without a territory. The first step to reclaiming your power is surviving the next twenty miles.

Player:
The Shadow Path (Woods) - Stick to the dense treeline parallel to the road. Slower movement, but Advantage on Stealth checks to avoid patrols.

Game Master:
You slip into the treeline, letting the dense canopy swallow you. The *Hunger*, satiated and purring, sharpens your senses to a razor's edge. Near midday, the terrain grows rockier. Your foot catches on a hidden root‚Äîa rare clumsiness (Stealth: 12)‚Äîand a branch snaps with a sound like a pistol crack. You freeze, melding into the shadow of a elm.

Nothing moves on the road. But your eyes, scanning the middle distance (Perception: 18), catch a discrepancy in the brush ahead. Thirty feet away, two figures are crouched behind a fallen log overlooking the road. They are **Bandits**, clad in mismatched leather and gripping rusty crossbows, waiting for a caravan to ambush.

But they aren't the only ones hunting. 

Your gaze shifts up, catching a slight sway in the branches above them. A third figure is perched there‚Äîa man with a scruffy beard and a predator's grin, balancing a dagger in his hand. He isn't with the bandits; he's hunting them.

**Assessment:** The stranger is skilled but arrogant. He creates chaos, which is useful, but he lacks your discipline. Currently, he provides a perfect flank.

**Looting the Dead:**

Tarnesh spins around, his hand snapping to his component pouch. But when he sees the lone, disheveled figure on the road, his tension morphs into sneering contempt. He relaxes his stance, though his hand hovers near his belt.

**The Departure.**

You meet **Jaheira** and **Khalid** at the main gate. The druid eyes your new armor with a critical nod, while Khalid seems relieved to see you fully equipped. The party of four strikes south along the Coast Way, leaving the sanctuary of the Friendly Arm behind.

The journey is a stark lesson in the region's decay. The road to Beregost is clogged with evidence of the Iron Crisis. You pass merchant wagons with shattered axles, the iron brittle and gray. You see refugees clutching farming tools that have snapped in half. The tension on the road is palpable; every traveler eyes the others with suspicion, hands hovering near weapons.

Your *Hunger* keeps you alert, scanning the treeline for threats, but the road is quiet today‚Äîlikely due to the heavy Flaming Fist patrols you spot periodically. Roric keeps pace easily, his earlier wounds forgotten, while Khalid and Jaheira walk with the synchronized rhythm of veteran partners.

By late afternoon, the sprawling town of **Beregost** appears on the horizon. It is a hub of trade, dominated by the massive temple of Lathander and the smoke of burning smithies. Even from here, you can hear the ring of hammers‚Äîsmiths desperately trying to forge iron that won't break.

"B-Beregost," Khalid stammers, wiping dust from his brow. "We should... we should rest here tonight. Thunderhammer Smithy is famous; perhaps they have news of the mines?"

You kneel briefly, not to mourn, but to harvest. You slash the leather thongs of her belt, securing a **Potion of Healing** and a vial of shimmering liquid‚Äî**Potion of Invisibility**. 

You move to **Khalid**. He lies face down, his hand still reaching for his wife. You check his pulse; silent. You tear a heavy pouch from his belt (**47 gold pieces**) and grab another **Potion of Healing** from his bandolier. His shield and armor are too heavy to strip in the chaos; you leave them as a monument to his failure.

"Garrick!" you bark, turning to the bard.

Garrick scrambles backward, his eyes wide with terror, trying to slip into the crowd. "No! Please! I didn't‚Äî"

You lunge for him, but the blood on the stones makes your footing slick, and the bard is slippery with fear. He dodges your grasp, stumbling toward the side street. 

**Roric** doesn't let him get far. The rogue sticks out a boot, sending Garrick sprawling face-first into the muck. Before the bard can scream, Roric has him by the collar of his motley tunic, a dagger pressed to his kidney.

"She said *come*," Roric hisses in his ear. "Walking is optional. Breathing is optional."

Garrick goes limp, sobbing quietly. "I'm coming! I'm coming!"

"Alleys! Now!" Roric shoves the bard toward the shadows.

You sprint into the labyrinth of Beregost's slums, the shouts of the Flaming Fist fading behind you. You are a fugitive, a murderer, and richer than you have ever been. The Harpers are dead. The contract is complete.

Player:
Find a Bolt-Hole - Roric is a rogue; ask him if he knows a safe house or a fence in Beregost.

Game Master:
The shouts of the Flaming Fist echo off the stone walls of the alley, but they are growing distant. The chaos you unleashed in the square acts as a smoke screen, pulling the eyes of the law toward the carnage while you slip through the veins of the city.

"Lead the way," you command.

***

**Kagain's Shop.**

The sun has set by the time you reach the unassuming storefront in the southern district. The sign above the door depicts a battered shield and a bag of gold. Roric picks the lock on the back door‚Äîa professional courtesy to avoid the street‚Äîand you slip inside, dragging the sobbing Garrick with you.

The interior smells of pipe tobacco, stale beer, and gun oil. Sitting behind a heavy desk littered with wanted posters is a dwarf with a beard like iron wire and eyes like flint. He has a heavy axe leaning against his chair and a loaded crossbow on the desk.

**Kagain** doesn't flinch as three bloodied fugitives break into his shop. He simply takes a drag from his pipe and exhales a cloud of blue smoke.

"You're bleeding on my floor," Kagain rumbles, his voice like gravel grinding together. "And judging by the noise uptown, you're the reason the Fist is running around like headless chickens."

He eyes the heavy purse at your belt, then the Harper cloak pin dangling from your pocket. A slow, greedy smile spreads across his face.

"I charge for privacy," the dwarf says, tapping the crossbow. "And I charge extra for Harper-killers. **100 gold** for the night. No questions asked. You can sleep in the cellar with the rats... and the rest of my inventory."

Player:
Recruit Kagain - Offer him a cut of the Nashkel job if he joins you. A tank would be useful.

Game Master:
You do not reach for your coin purse. Instead, you step further into the dim light of the shop, letting the door click shut behind you. You gesture to Roric, who dumps the sobbing Garrick onto a pile of grain sacks, then you turn your gaze to the dwarf.

"One hundred gold buys me a cellar and a sleepless night," you say, your voice smooth and reasonable. "But you didn't build a mercenary charter by renting out rooms, Kagain. You built it by recognizing opportunity."

You lean against his desk, resting your hand near the hilt of your weapon‚Äînot as a threat, but as a promise of capability. "The Harpers are dead because they let morality get in the way of efficiency. I don't have that problem. And neither do you."

Kagain's eyes narrow beneath his bushy brows, smoke curling from his pipe. He waits.

"We're heading south to Nashkel," you continue. "The mines are rotting. Everyone thinks it's demons or bad luck. I think it's profit waiting to be seized. I need a tank‚Äîsomeone who can hold a line while I dismantle the threats. You join us. You get an equal share of the loot, a cut of whatever we bleed from the mine owners, and the protection of the most efficient killers in Beregost."

**Persuasion Check: 22 (Success)**

Kagain stares at you for a long moment, chewing on the stem of his pipe. Then, a low, rumbling chuckle erupts from his chest. He leans forward, the wood of his chair creaking.

He stands, hefting his battleaxe with practiced ease. "Truth is, I've got business south anyway. Some noble brat from Baldur's Gate‚ÄîSilvershield's boy‚Äîwent missing with a caravan near the Coast Way. I took the contract to find him, but my last crew... well, they retired early. He spits on the floor. "I need bodies to clear the road. You need a shield. It's a deal. No room fee. We split the loot. But the Silvershield bounty is mine."

Roric grins from the corner, checking the edge of his scimitar. "Look at us. A regular company of heroes."

Player:
Recruit Kagain - Offer him a cut of the Nashkel job if he joins you. A tank would be useful.

Game Master:

Player:
Recruit Garrick (Force) - Terrify him into servitude. &quot;Join us or die.&quot; He adds arcane support and lore knowledge.

**Garrick has joined the party.**

With your team assembled‚Äîa thief, a mercenary, and a bard‚Äîyou settle in for the night. Kagain bars the door and extinguishes the lamps, plunging the shop into darkness. Player:
Talk to Roric - Spend some time bonding with the rogue before sleep. Discuss the heist.

Game Master:
The cellar is damp and smells of old wine and rust, a fitting barracks for a company of fugitives. Kagain has retreated upstairs to 'guard the door' (and likely count his own gold), leaving the three of you alone in the dark underbelly of the shop.

**Mirtul 4, Morning.**

You wake before dawn. The cellar is cold. Kagain is already awake, kicking Garrick awake with a grunt. "Up, squealer. We march."

The streets of Beregost are quiet, but the tension is palpable. Wanted posters will be going up soon. You need to be gone before the sun hits the cobblestones.

Player:
Stealth Departure - Stick to the back alleys and fields to avoid the town gates entirely.

Game Master:
The dawn mist clings to the cobblestones of Beregost, thick and grey, a shroud provided by the coast to cover your retreat. You lead the way, slipping out the back door of Kagain's shop into the narrow, refuse-choked alleyways. The town is waking up; you hear the distant creak of cart wheels and the bark of dogs, but the heavy tramping of the Flaming Fist patrols is what you listen for.

Your party is a motley collection of shadows. **Roric** moves with professional silence, scouting the corners. **Garrick** is pale and trembling, clutching his lute case like a shield, stepping exactly where you step. Surprisingly, **Kagain** is the most disciplined; despite his heavy mail, the dwarf moves with a surprising, rolling grace, knowing exactly how to keep his armor from clanking against the stone walls.

You skirt the edge of the market district. A fresh poster has been wheat-pasted to the wall of the Burning Wizard Inn. Even in the dim light, the charcoal sketch is undeniable: a woman with intense eyes and a longbow. *Wanted for Murder. 500 Gold Pieces.*

"They got your nose wrong," Roric whispers, glancing at it. "But the price is flattering."

"Quiet," you hiss.

You reach the southern perimeter. The main gate is heavily guarded; you can see the torches of six Fist soldiers checking wagons. Instead of the road, you cut through a tanner's yard. The smell of curing leather and lye burns your nose, masking your scent from the guard dogs.

There is a moment of tension near the fence line. A patrol passes on the other side, close enough that you can hear the jingle of their harness. Garrick's foot slips on a wet stone, sending a pebble skittering. The guard pauses. "Did you hear that?"

You freeze, your hand hovering over your dagger. Kagain shifts his weight, ready to violence. But a stray cat, sensing the tension, bolts from a pile of crates, drawing the guard's ire.

"Damn cats," the guard mutters, moving on.

You slip through a gap in the rotting fence and drop into the high grass of the fields beyond. You move low and fast until the walls of Beregost are a grey smudge in the distance. You have escaped.

**The Coast Way South.**

By midday, the adrenaline has faded, replaced by the rhythm of the march. The road to Nashkel stretches out before you, winding through the Cloudpeak Mountains. The terrain grows wilder here; the manicured farmlands of Beregost give way to rocky scrub and twisted pines.

Kagain walks point, his axe resting on his shoulder. "Nashkel is two days hard march," he grunts. "If we push, we can make the river crossing by nightfall. But this is hobgoblin country. They like to ambush travelers near the bridge."

Roric checks the sun. "We have supplies. We have weapons. And we have a bard who looks like he's about to faint. Maybe we set a pace that doesn't kill the softest link?"

Garrick wipes sweat from his brow. "I... I am fine! Just... unaccustomed to the heat."

You scan the horizon. The *Hunger* is quiet, but the *Satiated* clarity remains. You are free of the city, but the wilderness has its own laws.

Player:
Debrief Garrick - Use the travel time to finally get the full story on Silke and her connections.

Game Master:
The sun beats down on the Coast Way, baking the mud into hard ruts that threaten to twist ankles with every step. The landscape here is starker than the gentle hills of the Friendly Arm; the trees are gnarled, wind-bent things, and the Cloudpeak Mountains loom like a bruised wall on the southern horizon.

Kagain marches at the vanguard, his heavy dwarven constitution ignoring the heat, while Roric drifts at the rear, eyes scanning their backtrail for the glint of Flaming Fist armor. You walk in the center, setting a pace that keeps **Garrick** breathless but moving.

Garrick licks his cracked lips, glancing nervously at Kagain's axe. "She... she never gave a name. Just 'The Throne'. She met with men in iron-grey cloaks at the Burning Wizard two nights ago. They didn't speak like locals. They spoke like... soldiers."

By late afternoon, the roar of the river reaches your ears. The bridge ahead is a narrow stone span, ancient and moss-slick. Kagain stops, raising a fist. "Hobgoblin sign," he grunts, pointing to a smear of dark blood on a milestone. "Fresh."

**The March West.**

**Mirtul 7, Dawn.**

In the center of the stronghold are several large pits‚Äîfighting pits‚Äîand a series of cages suspended over a dark chasm.

Between you and her lies a small army. A frontal assault against fifty gnolls is suicide, even for Minsc. But the stronghold has weaknesses: the wooden walls are dry, the guards are undisciplined, and the cliffs above offer a sniper's perch.

**Mirtul 8, Midday.**

You are camped in a high alpine meadow, miles from the stronghold. The air is crisp and clean. **Dynaheir** sits by the fire, mending her robes with a needle and thread Roric 'found'. She looks up as you approach.

"You possess a rare quality for a leader," the witch says, studying you. "Restraint. Rashemen warriors often die because they do not know when to sheath the blade. You... you calculate the cost of blood."

She gestures to the south, where the peaks give way to the valley of Nashkel. "My journal... my research into the Iron Crisis... it was lost in the capture. But the knowledge is in my head. The 'taint' is alchemical, as your bard suspected. But it is old magic. Abyssal."

**Minsc** is sparring with **Kagain** nearby, the clang of steel ringing out. **Garrick** is furiously scribbling in a notebook, muttering about "The Ballad of the Burning Keep."

"We are a day's march from town," Roric says, chewing on a piece of dried meat. "We could head straight back to the Mayor and get that mine contract. Or... we could hunt. Game Master:
You turn your back on the direct road to Nashkel, leading your company east into the jagged foothills that border the mines. The terrain here is treacherous‚Äîshale slopes that slide underfoot and box canyons that trap the heat of the midday sun. But the *Hunger* pulls you forward, sensing a different kind of prey.

**Roric** scouts ahead, his mood improved by the promise of gold. "Sculptors," he mutters, checking the edge of his scimitar. "Why is it always artists stealing things? A blacksmith steals an anvil, I get it. But stealing rocks to carve rocks?"

**Dynaheir** walks with a quiet dignity, ignoring the rogue's commentary. She uses her staff to navigate the scree, her eyes scanning the horizon for magical anomalies. **Minsc** acts as her shadow, glaring at every shifting pebble as if it might threaten his charge.

By early afternoon, you hear it: the rhythmic *chink-chink-chink* of metal on stone, echoing off the canyon walls like a heartbeat.

You crest a rise and freeze. Before you, carved directly into the sheer face of a grey cliff, is a face of breathtaking, impossible beauty. It is an elven woman, her expression one of sorrow and grace, emerging from the mountain as if waking from a deep sleep. Even **Kagain** pauses, grunting in grudging respect.

Suspended on a rickety wooden scaffold in front of the carving is a gaunt, frantic elf. He is covered in stone dust, his hands moving in a blur as he chisels at the statue's cheekbone. This is **Prism**.

He spots you instantly. He does not reach for a weapon; he clutches a heavy velvet pouch at his belt to his chest.

"No!" Prism screams, his voice thin and desperate. "Not yet! I am not finished! You cannot take them!"

He points a trembling chisel at you. "She needs her eyes! The emeralds... they are for her! Queen Ellesime must see!"

**Roric** steps up beside you, eyeing the pouch. "That's the bounty, Nocturne. 300 gold for the gems, likely more for his head. And he's cornered."

**Minsc** frowns, looking up at the statue. "But... look, Boo. It is pretty. The stone-man loves the stone-lady. Is it evil to make art?"

Before you can decide the sculptor's fate, the sound of heavy, iron-shod boots crunching on gravel draws your attention to the trail behind you. A man steps out from the shadow of a boulder.

He is a professional. You can tell by the way he stands‚Äîbalanced, relaxed, dangerous. He wears heavy plate armor that gleams in the sun, and his hand rests on the hilt of a longsword that hums with a faint, magical vibration. His face is a mask of cold boredom.

"The artist dies today," the newcomer says, his voice a metallic rasp. "I am **Greywolf**. I have tracked this thief from Amn. Hand him over, along with the gems, and I will let you walk away with your lives."

He draws his sword. The blade glows with a cold, blue light (**Varscona +2**). It is a weapon worth a kingdom to a level 3 adventurer.

"Interfere," Greywolf adds, his eyes locking onto yours, "and I will carve my own statue from your bones."

You do not take the map. Instead, you let it hang in the air between you, suspended by the tension of your silence. You look around the opulence of the Temple‚Äîthe gold-inlaid altar of Helm, the fine vestments of the priest, the polished plate of the guards.

"The future of the Sword Coast," you repeat, your voice mocking. "That sounds expensive, Mayor. And 'slaughter' sounds messy."

You step closer, invading his personal space just as you did with Silke. The *Hunger* sharpens your gaze, dissecting his desperation. "You want me to walk into a hole in the ground that is eating your soldiers. You want me to kill something that scares a garrison of Amnish troops. That isn't charity work, Ghastkill. That is a contract."

You slam your hand onto the altar, right next to the map. "Two thousand gold pieces. One thousand now, to outfit my team. One thousand upon completion. Pay it, or send your guards down there to die."

**Intimidation Check: 16 (Success vs DC 15 / Failure vs DC 20)**

Ghastkill blanches, clutching the holy symbol at his neck. "Two... two thousand? Madwoman, the garrison hasn't been paid in a tenday! The trade routes are dead! We don't have that kind of coin in the entire town treasury!"

He looks at your face, expecting you to back down. You do not. You simply stare, the *Satiated* predator waiting for the prey to stop thrashing.

"I... I cannot give you two thousand," Ghastkill stammers, sweat beading on his bald pate. He looks frantically at the priest, then unlocks a heavy iron chest beneath the altar. "But I can give you everything we have left. **Nine hundred gold pieces**. Four hundred now‚Äîthat is every coin in this chest‚Äîand five hundred when you bring me the head of the leader."

He dumps a heavy sack onto the map. "Take it. Please. Just stop the killing."

It isn't the two thousand you demanded, but it is likely every copper piece the desperate town possesses. You weigh the sack in your hand. Heavy. Acceptable.

"Done," you say, snatching the map. "We leave in the morning. Try not to lose the rest of my money while I'm gone."

You turn to your party. **Roric** is grinning at the audacity. **Kagain** nods approvingly at the negotiation tactics. **Minsc** is confused but happy that evil will be kicked. **Dynaheir** looks weary, but ready.

You have the contract. You have the advance. You have the team. Now, you need to be at full strength to survive the dark.

**Kagain** laughs, a sound like grinding stones. "That's not fear, thief. That's respect. Finally, a leader who knows what blood is worth."

You stand on the steps of the Temple. The town is dark. The mines await to the south. You have **1,021 gold**, a full party, and a contract. But your spell slots are nearly empty, and the march has been long.

Game Master:
You do not leave the temple steps immediately. Instead, you turn to your pack, the *Hunger* guiding you to separate the useful tools from the potential liabilities.

**Strategy: Gaslight the Berserker**
You step into Minsc's line of sight, blocking his view of the Mayor's trembling form. You place a hand on the berserker's pauldron, looking up at him with a gaze of intense, martial respect.

"The Mayor pays us not for charity, Minsc, but because he recognizes a true force of nature," you say, your voice vibrating with conviction. "He knows that laws and courts have failed. He knows that the only thing that can scrub the darkness from those mines is your sword. You are not a mercenary today; you are the Hammer of Justice."

Minsc's chest swells, his earlier confusion about the extortion vanishing under the praise. "Justice! Yes! Boo says the coin is just fuel for the butt-kicking engine! We shall scrub the darkness until it sparkles!"

**Strategy: Isolate the Witch**
Before Dynaheir can interject with questions about the morality of threatening town officials, you pivot to her. You shove the map of the mines into her hands, effectively cutting off her line of sight to the others.

"Dynaheir, the Mayor mentioned Abyssal signatures," you lie smoothly, leveraging her academic curiosity. "I need you to cross-reference this layout with your knowledge of ley lines and planar breaches. Don't worry about the logistics or the gold; that is grunt work. Your mind is the only weapon sharp enough to dissect the *source* of the taint. Focus on that. Ignore everything else."

Dynaheir frowns, looking at the map, her ego stroked just enough to distract her. "Abyssal... yes. The geometry of the tunnels does seem... spiral. I will study it. Do not disturb me."

**The Investment**
With the party psychically managed, you lead them back to the **Nashkel General Store**. The shopkeeper groans as you enter, but the heavy sack of gold silences him.

You select gear with a cold, necrotizing logic: what makes them effective now, but remains valuable if they become... absent.

For **Minsc**, you purchase a suit of **Splint Mail (200 gp)**. It is heavy, durable, and expensive. It will keep him alive while he tanks for you, and if he dies, it can be stripped, cleaned, and sold‚Äîor worn by Kagain.

For **Dynaheir**, you ignore the scrolls she eyes longingly (which become useless ink once scribed) and instead purchase a **Wand of Magic Missiles (400 gp)**. It is a simple, brutal tool. It gives her burst damage now, but more importantly, it is a universal item. If the witch falls, **Garrick** can pick it up and use it instantly. It is an asset that belongs to the party, not the wizard.

"Equip yourselves," you order, tossing the gear to them. "We march on the mines tonight."

Minsc straps on the heavy armor, looking like a steel mountain. Dynaheir tests the balance of the wand, looking pleased despite herself. They are stronger. And you are ready to use them.

Game Master:
You leave the general store and cross the square to the **Northern Light Inn**. It is a warm, timber-framed sanctuary against the mountain chill, and you do not intend to sleep on straw tonight. You toss a pouch of **50 gold pieces** to the innkeeper, demanding the Royal Suite.

The room is opulent by frontier standards‚Äîfeather beds, a roaring hearth, and a private bath filled with steaming water. For the first time in days, the grit of the road is scrubbed from your skin. You eat a hot meal of roasted venison and spiced wine, the *Hunger* purring contentedly in the back of your mind.

**Minsc** and **Boo** take the rug by the fire, snoring in unison. **Kagain** claims the armchair, sharpening his new axe with rhythmic scrapes. **Dynaheir** sits by the window, meditating on the geometry of the mine map, while **Garrick** tunes his lute nervously. **Roric** sleeps with one eye open near the door.

You sleep deeply, the luxury of the suite mending the micro-tears in your muscle and spirit. When you wake at dawn, you feel invincible. The fatigue is gone. Your magic has returned. You are a blade honed to a razor's edge.

**Long Rest Complete.**

You assemble your pack in the courtyard as the sun crests the Cloudpeaks. The air is cold and smells of sulfur. South of the town, the gaping maw of the **Nashkel Mines** waits, a black scar in the earth. The workers are refusing to enter, huddled in groups near the entrance, whispering of demons.

Game Master:
You approach the huddle of miners gathered near the slag heaps. They are a sorry sight‚Äîmen and women with dust-choked lungs and hollow eyes, clutching pickaxes like weapons of war rather than tools of industry. They watch your approach with a mix of fear and desperate hope, eyeing the heavy plate on Minsc and the glowing rune on Kagain's new shield.

A burly man with a soot-stained beard, likely the foreman, steps forward. He spits a glob of black phlegm onto the frozen mud.

"More mercenaries?" he rasps. "Ghastkill keeps sending 'em. The mountain keeps eating 'em."

You stop a few paces away, letting the silence stretch just long enough to be uncomfortable. The *Hunger* sharpens your gaze, dissecting their terror. They aren't scared of a cave-in. They are scared of something hunting them.

"The Mayor paid us a great deal of gold to stop the eating," you say, your voice calm and professional. "But to do that, I need to know what's on the menu. You speak of demons. Be specific. Are we talking about fiends from the Abyss, or just something with sharp teeth?"

**Persuasion Check: 21 (Success)**

The foreman looks at your gear‚Äîthe enchanted sword at your hip, the confident set of your shoulders‚Äîand decides you might actually survive the first hour.

"Not demons in the holy sense, mistress," the foreman admits, lowering his voice. "But devils all the same. **Kobolds**. Hundreds of 'em. But not like any kobolds we've seen. They don't scatter when you yell. They hold the line. They set traps‚Äîtripwires, poison darts, fire bottles. And they yip... they yip like laughing hyenas while they stick you."

He shudders. "But that ain't the worst of it. Deep down? Third level and below? The kobolds don't go there. We hear... shuffling. Clanking. Like metal dragging on stone. And the smell... smells like a grave opened up in the summer heat. **Undead**. Skeletons, mostly, but armored. And they guard the iron."

**Insight Check: 15 (Success)**

You read the truth in his fear. The kobolds are the infantry‚Äîorganized, trapped, dangerous in numbers. The undead are the heavy guard, protecting the source of the taint deep in the earth. This confirms Dynaheir's theory of a higher intelligence directing them; kobolds and skeletons do not naturally ally.

**Minsc** growls low in his throat. "Kobolds? Little dog-men who fight with traps? Boo says this is cowardly! We shall stomp them like bugs!"

**Kagain** grunts. "Traps mean we watch our feet. Undead mean we bring blunt instruments. Skeletons don't bleed, but they shatter."

**Dynaheir** steps forward, her eyes scanning the dark tunnel entrance. "The air... it tastes metallic. And necrotic. The taint is strong here. We must be cautious."

You have the intel: **Kobolds (Traps/Ambush)** in the upper levels, **Undead** in the depths. The entrance looms before you, a dark maw breathing cold, foul air.

Player:
Solo Ghost Recon - Enter alone first using Umbral Sight. Map the first level and disable traps, then signal the party.

Game Master:
You leave the party at the mine entrance, a silent command keeping them back. The air grows colder as you step across the threshold, the light of dawn dying within twenty feet. To a human, this is blindness. To you, it is home.

Your **Umbral Sight** activates. The pitch-black tunnels shift into a monochrome landscape of greys and sharp contrasts. You see the rough-hewn walls, the rusted tracks of the ore carts, and the scurrying shapes of rats. More importantly, you see the **Kobolds**.

They are everywhere. Small, dog-like humanoids moving in efficient packs, carrying baskets of tainted ore. They chatter in yipping Draconic, their eyes glowing faintly red in the dark. But they do not see you. To their darkvision, you are nothing but empty air. You walk right past a sentry post, the guard sniffing the air suspiciously but seeing nothing.

**Infiltration Report:**
*   **The Layout:** The first level is a maze of support beams and narrow chokepoints. The central shaft is guarded by a heavy patrol.
*   **The Traps:** Your enhanced perception picks them out easily. A tripwire across the main thoroughfare (you step over it). A pressure plate hidden under loose shale (you mark it with a scrape of your boot). Without thieves' tools, you cannot dismantle the complex mechanisms, but you jam the triggers of the primitive traps with stones and cut the tension cords of the crossbow rigs.
*   **The Enemy:** You count at least three dozen kobolds on this level alone. They are armed with shortswords and light crossbows, utilizing "murder holes" drilled into the rock to fire on intruders from safety.

You reach a junction overlooking the main descent shaft. The path is clear of immediate mechanical danger. You backtrack silently to the entrance, emerging from the darkness like a wraith.

"The first level is a kill box," you report to the waiting party. "But I have jammed the triggers. The kobolds are reliant on darkvision; they won't see us until we are in melee range if we stick to the shadows. We can clear the upper tunnels quickly."

Player:

Game Master:
You lead the pack deeper into the earth, moving through the tunnels like a virus entering a bloodstream. The jamming of the traps has left the artery open, and your party flows through it silently. The air grows warmer, heavy with the smell of unwashed bodies and sulfur.

You reach the overlook of the **Main Excavation Chamber**. It is a massive natural cavern, reinforced with rotting beams. Below you, the heart of the infestation beats. Three dozen **Kobolds** are working the rock faces, their picks rising and falling in a jagged rhythm. They are overseen by a massive **Kobold Chieftain** sitting on a throne of ore, barking orders while gnawing on a bone. Near him, a shaman dances around a green fire.

They rely entirely on their darkvision in the gloom. To them, the upper gantry where you stand is empty shadow. To you, it is a shooting gallery.

"The big one is mine," you whisper. "Minsc, Kagain... the floor is yours."

**The Ambush.**

You step to the edge, the *Hunger* steadying your hand. You are invisible to them. You have Advantage. You have the element of dread.

**Twang.**

Your first arrow screams down from the dark. It is a perfect, hateful shot. The shaft takes the **Kobold Shaman** directly in the throat as he inhales to chant. His head snaps back, and he collapses into his own green fire, thrashing silently as the flames consume him.

**Twang.**

Before the Chieftain can even turn his head, your second arrow‚Äîfueled by the *Dread Ambusher* momentum‚Äîslams into his chest plate. It punches through the crude iron, burying itself in his lung (14 damage). He roars, falling off his throne, blood spraying the ore.

"JUSTICE RAINS FROM ABOVE!" **Minsc** bellows, leaping from the gantry. He hits the cavern floor with a bone-shaking impact, his greatsword already swinging. He cleaves a worker in two before he even straightens up.

**Kagain** follows, sliding down a scree slope on his shield like a sled, chopping the legs out from under a sentry as he passes.

**Roric** stays high, his bow singing a duet with yours, picking off the confused guards trying to rush the berserker.

The chamber explodes into chaos. The kobolds are screaming, their darkvision betraying them as death rains from the invisible dark.

Player:

Game Master:
You do not give the Chieftain time to breathe, let alone rally his kin. From your perch in the shadows, you draw and loose with the dispassionate rhythm of a metronome. The angle is steep, but the *Hunger* compensates.

The arrow streaks down into the torchlight. The Chieftain, struggling to push himself up from the ore pile, takes the shaft directly between his shoulder blades. He collapses back down with a wet grunt, pinned to the earth.

"The head is severed!" you signal.

**Minsc** acknowledges the kill with a roar. He stomps onto the prone leader, his heavy boot crushing the kobold's shield arm, and brings his greatsword down in a vertical chop that ends the Chieftain's command permanently.

**The Chieftain is dead.**

The effect on the chamber is immediate. The rhythm of the pickaxes stops. Thirty pairs of glowing red eyes look from the burning Shaman to the butchered Chieftain, and then up at the invisible terror raining death from the gantry. The pack bond fractures. Some of the kobolds are dropping their weapons, preparing to grovel. Others are backing toward the dark tunnels leading down, eyes darting nervously. A few diehards near the throne are snarling, desperate but leaderless.

**Short Rest**

The hour passes in tense silence, broken only by the dripping of condensation and the occasional settling of the mountain overhead. 

**Kagain** sits on a crate of ore, stripping off his dented armor to tend to the deep bruising on his side. **The Descent**

When the hour is up, you clear the barricade and move to the central shaft. The air drafting up from below is noticeably colder, carrying a metallic tang that tastes like old blood and ozone. This is not the musk of kobolds; this is the scent of the grave.

You descend the ladder first, slipping into the gloom of **Level 2**.

The architecture changes here. The rough-hewn tunnels of the kobolds give way to older, shored-up passages. The silence is absolute, heavy and oppressive. There is no yipping, no pickaxes striking stone.

Your **Umbral Sight** pierces the dark. The tunnel ahead opens into a large junction. The ground is littered with debris‚Äîshattered crates, rusted tools, and bones. Not kobold bones. Human bones. Gnawed and broken.

And standing sentinel at the far end of the junction, motionless as statues, are four figures. They wear the tattered remnants of Amnish guard uniforms, but the flesh has rotted away to reveal gleaming white bone. They hold rusted longswords and heavy shields. 

**Skeletons.**

But they are not alone. Behind them, lurking in the shadows of a side tunnel, you spot small, hunched shapes holding glass bottles that glow with a faint, sick green light. The "Green Bottles" the prisoner mentioned.

"Contact," you whisper. "Undead. And grenadiers."

Player:
Snipe grenadiers and try to trigger surprise round

Game Master:
You meld into the shadows of the tunnel wall, the *Umbral Sight* rendering you a ghost in the darkness. The skeletons stand rigid, their empty sockets fixed on the main passage, oblivious to the predator flanking them. Behind them, the kobold grenadiers bicker silently, clutching their volatile payloads.

You draw the **Arrow +1**, the magical fletching humming against your cheek. The *Hunger* slows time. You are not shooting at targets; you are removing variables from an equation.

**Twang.**

The first arrow hisses through the gap between two skeletons. It strikes the lead grenadier directly in the chest. The impact is catastrophic; the arrow punches through his ribs and shatters the spine. He drops instantly, the glass bottle in his hand rolling harmlessly across the stone floor.

**Dread Ambusher Activates.**

Before the first body hits the ground, you are already moving, the supernatural speed of the Gloom Stalker fueling your next shot. You shift your aim to the second grenadier, who is just beginning to turn his head.

**Twang.**

The second arrow strikes with even greater force, driven by the ambusher's momentum. It catches the kobold in the throat, lifting him off his feet and pinning him to the wooden support beam behind him. He thrashes once, then goes still.

**Both Grenadiers are down.**

The skeletons rattle, turning their skulls slowly toward the source of the death, but they are mindless automatons, slow to react. They have not even drawn their weapons. You have the initiative, the element of surprise, and a clear path to the undead.

"The backline is clear!" you signal. "Crush the bones!"

Player:
Kagain Shield Bash - Send the dwarf in to bowl them over with his heavy shield, creating a prone pile for easy execution.

Game Master:
"Kagain!" you bark. "Bowl them over!"

The dwarf does not hesitate. He sees the line of skeletons standing rigid in the gloom, their shields raised but their reaction times slowed by centuries of rot. He grunts, lowers his shoulder behind his massive new steel shield, and charges.

It is like watching a boulder roll through a picket fence. Kagain hits the center of the formation with the force of a runaway cart. The impact is deafening‚Äîa crunch of bone and iron that echoes down the corridor.

**Shield Bash Success.**

**The Return.**

The ascent is grueling but unopposed. You leave the darkness of the mines behind, emerging into the blinding afternoon sun of the Cloudpeaks. The air tastes sweet after the sulfur of the pit.

By the time you reach the town square, the mood has shifted. The sullen fear is gone, replaced by a buzzing, nervous energy. He stands on the steps, wringing his hands, looking terrified that you might have failed‚Äîor perhaps more terrified that you succeeded and he now owes you a fortune.

You throw Mulahey's holy symbol at his feet. It clatters loudly against the white stone.

"The mines are clear," you say, the *Hunger* projecting an aura of absolute dominance. "The cleric is dead. The kobolds are scattered. Now, pay me."

The party is gathered. Roric and Xan have returned with the supplies. The map to the **Cloakwood Mines** points northwest, into the deep forest. The proxy mission was a success, but lingering here risks discovery by the Flaming Fist patrols scouring the countryside.

Game Master:
You refuse to accept the inefficiency of the first attempt. You plunge back into the undergrowth, the *Hunger* driving you to find a replacement for the wasted venom.

Game Master:
You retrieve the **Chain Mail +1** from the pile. The links are incredibly fine, shimmering with a faint, verdant light in the gloom of the armory. 

"Xan," you call out. The elf looks up from his cleaning, his face a mask of weary resignation. You toss the bundle of mail to him. "Put it on. If you're going to complain about impending doom, you might as well be dressed for it."

Xan catches the armor, his eyes widening as he runs a long finger over the weave. "Mithral," he breathes. "And woven with the enchantments of Evereska. This is Elven Chain. It breathes with the wearer... it will not hinder the somatic gestures of the Art."

He strips off his tattered grey robes and dons the mail. It fits him perfectly, clinking softly as he moves. He draws his Moonblade, the blue light reflecting off the silver links. For the first time, he looks less like a doomed scholar and more like a battle-mage of the elven courts. "I... I suppose this improves my odds of survival from 'none' to 'negligible'. Thank you."

With the party equipped, you turn your attention to the structure itself. The Armory is built of sturdy stone, defensible and dry. The rest of the camp is a smoking ruin, but this building can be held.

"We are not leaving," you announce. "We are digging in."

**Operation: Stronghold**

For the next several hours, you direct the fortification efforts with the ruthless efficiency of a siege engineer.

*   **The Walls:** **Kagain** and **Minsc** use their strength to drag heavy iron weapon racks and stone debris to the windows and the breached rear hatch, creating firing slits that offer heavy cover while blocking entry.
*   **The Perimeter:** You and **Roric** sweep the immediate area. You reset the bandits' own bear traps in the tall grass and string tripwires with bells across the approach paths. 
*   **The Wards:** **Dynaheir** uses chalk to inscribe glyphs of warning on the main threshold. "They will not pass unseen," she promises.

By sunset, the Armory has been transformed. It is no longer a loot cache; it is a Forward Operating Base. You have a secure location to rest, store supplies, and retreat to if the Cloakwood proves too deadly.

"A fortress!" Minsc declares, planting his boot on a barricade. "Boo says it needs a name! The Hamster Hold? The Butt-Kicking Bastion?"

"The Armory," you correct him flatly. "It keeps our steel dry and our enemies out."

You stand on the roof of your new stronghold, looking northwest toward the brooding canopy of the **Cloakwood**. The sun is setting behind the trees, casting long, spider-legged shadows across the valley. You have a base. You have an army. The hunt begins now.

**The Long Night**

The Armory is warm and dry, a stone womb protecting you from the wind howling through the ruins of the camp outside. You do not sleep immediately. Instead, you sit by the hearth, stripping your mind of the city and the desert, retuning your spirit to the frequency of the deep woods.

The *Hunger* aids you, shedding the aggressive, fast-twitch magic of *Zephyr Strike* and the urban utility of *Disguise Self*. In their place, you weave new instincts into your blood. You meditate on the chittering of spiders and the slow, crushing growth of roots. You learn the tongue of beasts and the magic of thorns.

**Spells Prepared:**
*   **Speak with Animals:** To turn the forest's denizens into spies.
*   **Spike Growth:** To turn the forest floor into a shredder.

When dawn breaks, you are no longer a raider; you are a warden of the wild.

**Mirtul 11, Morning**

You march at first light. The journey northwest is a descent into a primal, suffocating green. The trees of the **Cloakwood** are ancient, their boughs woven together so tightly that the sun is reduced to a sickly twilight. The air is heavy with moisture and the smell of rot.

By midday, the signs of the **Spider Nest** are undeniable. Thick, sticky webbing spans between the colossal elms, trapping birds, deer, and the occasional unlucky bandit. The ground is soft, muffling your footsteps, but the silence is heavy, broken only by the skittering of many legs high in the canopy.

**Dynaheir** shudders, pulling her robes tight. "The Weave is sticky here. Distorted. There is a malice in these webs."

**Minsc** draws his blade, peering into the gloom. "Boo does not like the look of that fly. It is too big. And it is wearing shoes."

You hold up a hand. Ahead, the path is blocked by a wall of webbing thick as rope. Through the gaps, you see movement‚Äîhuge, bulbous shapes descending from the trees. **Giant Spiders**. And leading them, a humanoid shape with a chitinous carapace‚Äîan **Ettercap** shepherd.

They have not seen you yet. Your *Pass Without Trace* (if cast) or natural stealth has held.
