**Strategic Analysis: The Cost of Waiting**

If you wait **5 days** for Garrick to arrive:
*   **The Stronghold:** Garrick will secure the base with mercenaries. It becomes a permanent asset, potentially generating resources or acting as a safe haven for Act 2.
*   **The Enemy:** The Iron Throne is not idle. In five days, news of the camp's fall may reach Davaeorn. He will fortify the Cloakwood Mines. The element of surprise will be lost, and the perimeter patrols will likely double.
*   **The Hunger:** This is the critical variable. You have approximately **6 days** of *Satiated* clarity remaining. Waiting burns five of them. You would enter the Cloakwood‚Äîa Tier 2-3 dungeon‚Äîon the verge of *Withdrawal*. You would need to hunt immediately or face the -2 penalty during the infiltration.

If you **March Now**:
*   **The Stronghold:** You leave the Armory trapped but empty. There is a significant chance (50%) it will be looted by scavengers or reclaimed by monsters before Garrick arrives.
*   **The Momentum:** You strike while the trail is hot. You arrive at the mines with your *Satiated* buff fully active for the duration of the crawl.

**Mirtul 12: The March**

You march at dawn. The journey northwest is a descent into a primal, suffocating green. The trees of the **Cloakwood** are ancient, their boughs woven together to block out the sun. The air is heavy with moisture and the smell of rot.

By midday, you reach the perimeter marked on Ender Sai's map. The forest here is draped in thick, sticky webbing that spans between the trees like the rigging of a ghost ship. The silence is profound, broken only by the chittering of things that have too many legs.

**Dynaheir** stops, her staff glowing faintly. "The Weave is sticky here. Distorted. There is a malice in these webs."

**Minsc** draws his blade, peering into the gloom. "Boo does not like the look of that fly. It is too big. And it is wearing shoes."

You hold up a hand. Ahead, the path is blocked by a wall of webbing thick as rope. Through the gaps, you see movement‚Äîhuge, bulbous shapes descending from the trees. **Giant Spiders**. And leading them, a humanoid shape with a chitinous carapace‚Äîan **Ettercap** shepherd.

They have not seen you yet. Your *Pass Without Trace* (if cast) or natural stealth has held.

**Dread Ambusher.**

The third arrow, fueled by the dread momentum, flies straight and true at the center mass. But Davaeorn twists, and the shaft passes through the final illusion, dispersing it in a flash of light.

**All Mirror Images Destroyed.**

Davaeorn stands alone, his magical protections stripped away in a single heartbeat. He blinks, realizing he is naked to the steel coming his way. He opens his mouth to scream a command word, to trigger a contingency, to *teleport*.

But you are faster.

**Initiative: Nocturne (28) vs Davaeorn (7).**

The wizard is still reeling from the surprise. He cannot raise a *Shield* spell. He cannot *Blink*. He is flat-footed and mortal. You have a full round of actions before he can take a single breath.

**Twang.**

**Twang.**

Davaeorn is bloodied (36/60 HP), but his eyes burn with manic fury. He raises a hand, sparks of lightning dancing between his fingers. "You insects! I will burn you to ash!"

**The Short Rest**

**Minsc** sits heavily on the plush carpet, wincing as he strips off his battered armor. He pats Boo gently. "A few scratches, little friend. Nothing a good nap and a sturdy bandage cannot fix!" He spends the hour tending to his wounds, his vitality returning with surprising speed.

**Dynaheir** claims Davaeorn's desk, spreading out the scrolls and potions you recovered. She works with the methodical precision of the Wychlaran, identifying the magical properties of the loot while nursing her own injuries.

"This potion," she says, holding up the swirling grey vial found in the cache. "**Potion of Storm Giant Strength**. It grants the strength of a titan for a short time. A devastating tool for our berserker, perhaps?"

She examines the **Potion of Master Thievery**. "And this... liquid shadow. It enhances agility and lockpicking skills to supernatural levels."

**Xan** sits by the unlit hearth, polishing his Moonblade. "We are alive," he murmurs, sounding disappointed. "Remarkable. Though now we must walk all the way back to Baldur's Gate. I assume the road will be paved with more bandits and spiders?"

**Roric** is busy stuffing silverware into his pack. "Let's hope so. Spiders don't carry gold, but bandits do."

By the time the hour is up, the party is restored. The wounds are bound, the magic is identified, and the loot is secured. You stand in the center of the room, the *Hunger* quiet but watchful. The mine is yours. The Iron Throne's operation here is ended.

"We are done," you announce. "The slaves go free. Then we march north."

Game Master:
You sit in Davaeorn's high-backed chair, fingers tracing the wood of the map table. The mine above you is silent, save for the dripping of water and the distant, fearful shuffling of the slaves on the upper levels. The *Hunger* looks at the infrastructure of the Iron Throne‚Äîthe tunnels, the equipment, the captive workforce, the defensible location‚Äîand sees not a dungeon to be cleared, but an asset to be seized.

The Iron Crisis has driven the price of ore to astronomical heights. If you were to simply... *stop* adding the poison, this mine would become a fountain of gold. The slaves are already broken; they fear the whip, and you hold the whip now.

Game Master:
You pull Roric aside, leading him to the corner of the sanctum where Davaeorn‚Äôs personal ledger sits open. The *Hunger* vibrates with the audacity of the gamble. You are about to trade your most useful tool for a kingdom.

"Roric," you murmur, your voice too low for the paladin-ears of Minsc to catch. "You like gold. You like power. How would you like to own a mine?"

Roric blinks, looking from the ledger to you. "Own? You mean occupy. Until the Fist arrives."

"The Fist is weeks away," you counter. "I'm leaving you here. You're the foreman now. You hold the fort. You manage the... workforce. You sell the ore to the Zhentarim contacts we found in Davaeorn's notes. Fifty percent is yours. The rest goes to the company."

The rogue's eyes narrow, calculating. "And the do-gooders?"

"Leave them to me."

You turn back to the party, your face settling into a mask of grim, heroic necessity. **Minsc** and **Dynaheir** are waiting, looking expectantly at the lift.

"We cannot leave the mine unguarded," you announce, your voice heavy with feigned concern. "If we leave, the Iron Throne will return within days. They will slaughter the workers we just freed. Someone must stay behind to organize their defense and fortify the entrance until we can send a garrison from Baldur's Gate."

You place a hand on Roric's shoulder. "Roric has volunteered. He will hold the line."

**Deception Check: 24 (Success)**

Minsc's eyes well up with tears. He grabs Roric in a bone-crushing hug. "Brave little sneak-man! You have the heart of a hamster! Guard them well! Boo salutes you!"

Dynaheir looks suspicious, her eyes darting between you and the rogue, but the logic holds. "It is... a noble sacrifice," she admits slowly. "The workers are vulnerable. Very well. We shall march to the city and strike the head of the snake."

**Roric has left the party.**

He gives you a final, knowing wink as he settles into Davaeorn's chair. "Don't keep me waiting too long, boss. I'm not a miner."

You ascend the lift one last time. You bypass the slaves on Level 1, telling them that "Administrator Roric" is now in charge of their safety. You exit the waterfall into the clean air of the Cloakwood.

The march north to **Baldur's Gate** begins. You are down a rogue, but you are up a fortress.

**Chapter 5: The City of Lies**

The journey takes five days. The road is hard, but your party is hardened. By **Mirtul 17**, the massive walls of Baldur's Gate rise from the fog like a cliff face. The city is a hive of intrigue, wealth, and corruption. And somewhere inside, the leaders of the Iron Throne are waiting.

But the gates are closed to all but residents and authorized caravans due to the Bandit crisis. You stand at the **Wyrm's Crossing** bridge, looking at the blockade.

"Halt!" a Flaming Fist guard barks. "City's closed. Turn back, or show your papers."

**Operation: Garrison Swap**

**Mirtul 12-14: The Return Trek**
You leave Roric with the keys to the kingdom and a warning not to get stabbed by the slaves. The march back to the **Bandit Camp** is swift; you know the terrain now, and the spiders are burned out. You arrive at the **Fortified Armory** on the evening of the 14th.

**The Rendezvous**
Your timing is impeccable. **Garrick** has just arrived from Nashkel, looking exhausted but triumphant. Trailing behind him are a dozen hard-looking mercenaries‚Äîunemployed caravan guards and Flaming Fist deserters looking for coin. He has followed your instructions to the letter.

"Mistress!" Garrick cries, dropping his pack. "The fortress is... rustic. But defensible! I have brought the swords you asked for!"

"Change of plan," you announce, not breaking stride. "This camp is a husk. The real prize is north. Pack up. We move the garrison to the Cloakwood."

Garrick's face falls. "But... my feet..."

"Walk," **Kagain** growls.

**Mirtul 15-17: The Deployment**
You lead the mercenary column back through the forest. With a dozen swords at your back, the few remaining beasts of the Cloakwood give you a wide berth. You arrive back at the **Cloakwood Mines** on the 17th.

**The Handoff**
You descend to Level 4. Roric is waiting, looking bored, tossing a dagger at a target drawn on a tapestry. He sees Garrick and the soldiers and grins.

"Relief!" Roric cheers, springing from the chair. "And not a moment too soon. The damp down here plays hell with my leathers."

You install **Garrick** as the Warden of the Mines. You give him simple orders: Hold the facility. Protect the workers. Stockpile the iron. Wait for your word to flood the market.

Garrick looks at the opulent sanctum, then at the army at his command. His chest swells. "Warden Garrick... I like the sound of that. I shall compose an anthem for our new domain!"

**Roric** rejoins the pack, equipping his gear. "Good to be back on the road, boss. Running a business is harder work than killing people."

You stand at the mine entrance. The asset is secured. The income is inevitable. Your party is whole again. The road to **Baldur's Gate** lies north, and the *Hunger* is beginning to stir again.

**The March North.**

By the evening of **Mirtul 19**, the stone walls of the Friendly Arm fortress rise from the dusk. It is a sanctuary of warmth and light compared to the dark woods. You pass the guards without incident and enter the courtyard.

**Bentley Mirrorshade** greets you at the bar, his eyes widening as he takes in your battered but upgraded gear. "You look like you've walked through the Hells and back," the gnome says, wiping a glass. "And you look like you have coin to spend."

"We do," you state. "But I want to see the good stock. No rust. No junk."

Bentley nods and unlocks the heavy iron cabinet behind the bar. He lays out a selection of high-quality goods.

The Iron Throne isn't happy about their mines. They've tightened the blockade at Wyrm's Crossing. No one gets in without papers or a bribe heavy enough to sink a galley."

**The Long Rest**

You spend the night in the inn's best suite, the luxury a stark contrast to the damp stone of the mines. **Minsc** snores loudly by the fire, Boo curled on his chest. **Kagain** counts his share of the loot again, just to be sure. **Dynaheir** and **Xan** discuss magical theory in hushed tones, the elf predicting doom while the witch outlines strategies for breaching magical wards.

**Roric** cleans his new magical shortsword, looking restless. "We're rich, boss. We could retire. Buy a ship. Sail to Waterdeep."

"We're not done," you reply, staring into the fire. The *Hunger* is quiet, but you can feel the edges of it fraying. The *Satiated* clarity is fading. You have hours, maybe a day, before the itch returns.

**Mirtul 16, Morning.**

You gather the pack in the courtyard as the sun burns off the morning mist. The road to **Baldur's Gate** stretches north, a ribbon of mud and danger. You have the Mayor's letter, the Iron Throne's documents, and a small army at your back.

"To the city!" Minsc cheers, brandishing his sword at a passing seagull. "Evil hides behind walls, but walls cannot stop justice! Or hamsters!"

"The blockade waits," Xan sighs. "Guards, bribes, and inevitable bureaucracy. I can hardly wait."

Player:
Hunt on the Road - Spend time hunting beasts along the Coast Way to refresh the Satiated timer before reaching the city.

Game Master:
You lead the pack away from the safety of the Friendly Arm, your eyes scanning the tree line not for threats, but for sustenance. The *Hunger* is a dull ache behind your eyes, a reminder that your clarity is borrowed time.

"The road is too quiet," you murmur to Roric. "The Iron Throne has cleared the way for their own wagons, but they leave eyes in the dark."

You drift into the woods, the *Pass Without Trace* spell weaving shadows around you. With a Survival check of **24**, the forest opens its secrets to you. You find tracks in the soft loam‚Äîheavy boots, not made for walking but for stalking. **Hobgoblins**.

You track them to a ridge overlooking the trade way. Two scouts, clad in the rusty chainmail of the Chill, are watching a merchant caravan trundle past. They never hear you approach.

It is quick. Efficient. You take the first one with an arrow through the throat; Roric silences the second with a blade to the kidney. As the life fades from the goblinoid's eyes, the ache in your head vanishes. The world snaps back into crystal-clear focus. The *Hunger* is fed.

**Satiated Refreshed (7 Days).**

By late afternoon, the massive stone span of **Wyrm's Crossing** looms out of the mist. It is a bridge-city, a chaotic sprawl of shops and shanties clinging to the ancient arches that span the River Chionthar. Beyond it, the massive walls of **Baldur's Gate** rise like a cliff face.

But the way is barred.

A heavy blockade of **Flaming Fist** soldiers blocks the entrance to the bridge. They are checking papers, searching wagons, and turning back anyone who looks like a refugee or a bandit. The tension is high; hands hover near sword hilts.

"Halt!" a Fist sergeant barks as you approach, eyeing your party's heavy gear and the bloodstains that never quite wash out of Kagain's armor. "City's closed by order of Grand Duke Eltan. No entry without a writ of passage or a damn good reason."

Minsc bristles. "We have a reason! Evil needs kicking in the city! And we have very large boots!"

Xan sighs. "We are going to be arrested. Again."

Player:
Present Documents - Show the Letter from Mayor Ghastkill and the Iron Throne intel. Demand entry on official business.

Game Master:
You produce the scroll case, sliding the heavy parchment across the barricade. The sergeant takes it with a scowl, his thumb rubbing the wax seal of Nashkel. He reads slowly, his lips moving with the words, but his expression shifts from suspicion to surprise as he reaches the section detailing the liberation of the mines.

He looks up, eyeing the bloodstains on Kagain's armor and the sheer size of Minsc's sword with new respect. Then he scans the letters signed by Tazok and Davaeorn.

"Iron Throne," the sergeant mutters, tapping the paper. "Commander Scar has been screaming about them for weeks. If this is real..."

He hands the documents back, snapping a salute that is only half-mocking. "Open the gate! These aren't refugees. They're official business."

The heavy iron portcullis grinds upward. The blockade parts. You step onto the bridge proper, the massive city of **Baldur's Gate** looming above you. It is a sprawling metropolis of grey stone and slate roofs, choking on the smoke of a thousand chimneys. The streets are teeming with people, noise, and the smell of commerce and corruption.

"We are in," **Xan** sighs, adjusting his moonblade. "Out of the frying pan, into the blast furnace. I expect we shall be poisoned by a noble within the hour."

**Minsc** gazes up at the high walls, wide-eyed. "So many butts! Boo does not know where to start kicking! We must find the biggest evil and start there!"

**Kagain** grunts, eyeing a passing merchant caravan. "First, we find an ale. Then we find a fence. This city smells like money."

A runner from the gate catches up to you as you enter the East District. "Wait! The Sergeant sent word ahead. **Commander Scar** of the Flaming Fist requests your presence at the Seven Suns trading coster. He says it's urgent."

**Mirtul 11: The Day of Preparation**

The wind howls through the ruined palisades, but inside your stone sanctuary, the preparations are methodical and grim. **Mirtul 12: The March**

You march at dawn. The journey northwest is a descent into a primal, suffocating green. The trees of the **Cloakwood** are ancient, their boughs woven together to block out the sun. The air is heavy with moisture and the smell of rot.

By midday, you reach the perimeter marked on Ender Sai's map. The forest here is draped in thick, sticky webbing that spans between the trees like the rigging of a ghost ship. The silence is profound, broken only by the chittering of things that have too many legs.

**Dynaheir** stops, her staff glowing faintly. "The Weave is sticky here. Distorted. There is a malice in these webs."

**Minsc** draws his blade, peering into the gloom. "Boo does not like the look of that fly. It is too big. And it is wearing shoes."

You hold up a hand. Ahead, the path is blocked by a wall of webbing thick as rope. Through the gaps, you see movement‚Äîhuge, bulbous shapes descending from the trees. **Giant Spiders**. And leading them, a humanoid shape with a chitinous carapace‚Äîan **Ettercap** shepherd.

They have not seen you yet. Your *Pass Without Trace* (if cast) or natural stealth has held.
